        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.4c12929"><meta property="og:title" content="Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c12929/asset/images/acsami.4c12929.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Iron based Prussian blue analogues (Fe-PBA) hold significant promise cathode materials for sodium ion batteries due to their low cost and desirable electrochemical properties. However, their practical application is often hindered by the presence of vacancy defects and issues of oxidation that arise during the material preparation process. To overcome these challenges, this study introduces an innovative T-shaped collision microreactor aimed at promoting a uniform concentration field, narrowing the gap between material mixing rate and reaction rate, and providing an oxygen-free environment for the synthesis of Fe-PBA. Employing this microreactor, Fe-PBAs were synthesized with a meticulous approach that led to a material possessing a well-defined morphology and a stoichiometry of Na1.54Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.93. The material exhibited a notable reduction in vacancy defects and minimized oxidation levels. Upon electrochemical evaluation, the Fe-PBA crafted within the microreactor demonstrated an impressive specific capacity of 94.1 mAh/g at a current density of 0.5 C and showcased a long-term cyclability with 72.6% capacity retention over 2000 cycles. Comparative analysis revealed that the structural and electrochemical properties of  Fe-PBA prepared in the microreactor outperformed those of samples prepared using traditional reactors. This work provides a new approach for the continuous and stable fabrication of high-performance battery cathode materials."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c12929/asset/images/acsami.4c12929.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '9d3f203e-b83c-4d62-b615-f29867d7a87e'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

src="https://www2.snapengage.com/chatjs/ServiceGetConfig?w=921a4ec7-cecf-43a6-afa5-6cd1346520b1"></script><script type="osano/blocked" async=""></script><script charset="utf-8" src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        });</script><style type="text/css">.MathJax_Hover_Frame {border-radius: .25em; -webkit-border-radius: .25em; -moz-border-radius: .25em; -khtml-border-radius: .25em; box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -webkit-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -moz-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -khtml-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; border: 1px solid #A6D ! important; display: inline-block; position: absolute}

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c12929&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsami.4c12929" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite <script nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Synthesis of Iron-Based Prussian Blue Analogues with Ultralong Cycle Performance in a Novel T-Shaped Collision Microreactor", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.4c12929", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Phosphorus Resources, School of Chemical Engineering, Sichuan University, Chengdu, Sichuan 610065, China</div></div><span class="conrtib-corresp"><strong>*</strong>E-mail: <a Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c12929/asset/images/medium/am4c12929_0013.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c12929/asset/images/large/am4c12929_0013.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c12929&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Iron based Prussian blue analogues (Fe-PBA) hold significant promise cathode materials for sodium ion batteries due to their low cost and desirable electrochemical properties. However, their practical application is often hindered by the presence of vacancy defects and issues of oxidation that arise during the material preparation process. To overcome these challenges, this study introduces an innovative T-shaped collision microreactor aimed at promoting a uniform concentration field, narrowing the gap between material mixing rate and reaction rate, and providing an oxygen-free environment for the synthesis of Fe-PBA. Employing this microreactor, Fe-PBAs were synthesized with a meticulous approach that led to a material possessing a well-defined morphology and a stoichiometry of Na<sub>1.54</sub>Fe[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>]<sub>0.93</sub>. The material exhibited a notable reduction in vacancy defects and minimized oxidation levels. Upon electrochemical evaluation, the Fe-PBA crafted within the microreactor demonstrated an impressive specific capacity of 94.1 mAh/g at a current density of 0.5 C and showcased a long-term cyclability with 72.6% capacity retention over 2000 cycles. Comparative analysis revealed that the structural and electrochemical properties of  Fe-PBA prepared in the microreactor outperformed those of samples prepared using traditional reactors. This work provides a new approach for the continuous and stable fabrication of high-performance battery cathode materials.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D53980%26pageCount%3D14%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DYiping%2BWang%252C%2BYang%2BJin%252C%2BYanjun%2BZhong%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D40%26contentID%3Dacsami.4c12929%26title%3DSynthesis%2Bof%2BIron-Based%2BPrussian%2BBlue%2BAnalogues%2Bwith%2BUltralong%2BCycle%2BPerformance%2Bin%2Ba%2BNovel%2BT-Shaped%2BCollision%2BMicroreactor%26numPages%3D14%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D53993%26publicationDate%3DOctober%2B2024" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2024 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries"> Batteries </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290693&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Crystals"> Crystals </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials"> Materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290652&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Microreactors"> Microreactors </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291251&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Sodium"> Sodium </a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Prussian+Blue+Analogues&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Prussian%20blue%20analogues">Prussian blue analogues</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Cathode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_cathode">cathode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Microreactor&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_microreactor">microreactor</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Cyclic+Stability&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_cyclic%20stability">cyclic stability</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Battery&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20battery">sodium-ion battery</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">In recent years, multiscale energy storage systems (ESSs) have undergone significant advancements, with energy storage secondary batteries serving as their core. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> However, the widespread use of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), the heart of these energy storage systems, has been hindered by dwindling lithium resources and escalating production costs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 3 and 4">(3,4)</a> Notably, sodium, a member of the Li family, possesses physical and chemical properties similar to those of Li. What sets it apart is its abundance in the crust, which is 423 times that of lithium, and its significantly lower price, which is only 1/186 of lithium’s. In addition, the operational mechanism of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) is essentially identical to that of LIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 5 and 6">(5,6)</a> However, SIBs utilize less expensive aluminum foil as the current collector for both the positive and negative electrodes, further enhancing cost-effectiveness. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7,8)</a> Among the emerging battery materials, including potassium ion batteries and magnesium ion batteries, SIBs exhibit the greatest potential in meeting the requirements of performance, cost, and scalability requirements. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref8 ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 8 and 9">(8,9)</a> Consequently, SIBs are  ideal replacement products for LIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p">The cathode material serves a critical component that determines energy density and cost of SIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10" aria-label="reference 10">(10)</a> Over the past decade, SIB cathode materials have witnessed significant advancements, leading to improved electrochemical performance. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> Currently, various cathode materials have been developed and utilized for SIBs, including layered oxides, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref12 ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref10 ref12 ref13" aria-label="reference 10, 12 and 13">(10,12,13)</a> polyanionic compounds <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14 ref15 ref16" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14 ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 14 to 16">(14−16)</a> and Prussian blue analogues (PBA). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref17 ref18" aria-label="reference 17 and 18">(17,18)</a> Among them, the PBA Na<sub>2</sub>M[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>] (M = Fe, Co, Ni, Mn, Cu, etc.) have garnered widespread attention due to their high energy density, good sustainability, and simple preparation process. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22" aria-label="reference 19 to 22">(19−22)</a> In particular, iron-based Prussian blue analogues (Na<sub>2</sub>Fe[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>], Fe-PBA) are dual electron redox reaction materials with a theoretical capacity of up to 170 mAh/g ─ a figure comparable to that of lithium iron phosphate cathode materials. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 23 and 24">(23,24)</a> Currently, the preparation methods of Fe-PBA mainly include the hydrothermal method, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> single iron source method <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> and liquid-phase precipitation method. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref19 ref27 ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref19 ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 19, 27 and 28">(19,27,28)</a> However, the hydrothermal and single iron source methods consume a lot of energy and produce highly toxic byproducts such as HCN. Therefore, the green and convenient liquid-phase precipitation method is an ideal preparation technique. Yan et al. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28" aria-label="reference 28">(28)</a> used a mixture of different NaCl to trisodium citrate ratios as a sodium additive and prepared Fe-PBA with high sodium content and low defects using a liquid-phase coprecipitation method. The material exhibited a first discharge specific capacity of 140 mAh/g at a current density of 0.2 C. It also demonstrated a superior rate capability with 55.2% of its initial capacity at 10 C and remarkable long-term cyclability with 78% capacity retention over 3700 cycles, highlighting its exceptional cycling stability. Nevertheless, there remain two significant challenges in the preparation of Fe-PBA. First, the mixing rate between Fe<sup>2+</sup> and [Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>]<sup>4–</sup> does not match the rapid reaction rate, leading to uneven mixing in traditional reactors, resulting in the formation of [Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>]<sup>4–</sup> vacancies in the final product. This, in turn,  compromises the structural stability of the material. Second, The traditional method for preparing battery materials is the one-pot method, which is an intermittent process. The product quality varies between different batches, and the Fe-PBA preparation process requires the introduction of N<sub>2</sub> as a protective gas. While the former issue can be partially addressed by adding chelating agent sodium citrate to slow release Fe<sup>2+</sup>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> the latter remains a concern. Despite Lim et al.’s <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> attempt to mitigate oxidation by incorporating ascorbic acid as an antioxidant, oxidation issues persist.</div><div class="NLM_p">Addressing the aforementioned challenges in Fe-PBA production lies in enhancing the mixing of the two liquid phase reactants and ensuring air isolation. Utilizing microreactors for the preparation process offers an ideal solution. On the one hand, numerous studies have shown that microreactors can enhance internal mixing, providing a homogeneous and stable environment for crystal nucleation and growth. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30 ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 30 to 32">(30−32)</a> On the other hand, reactions within microreactors are continuous and enclosed by liquid, effectively eliminating air exposure. To date, research on the use of microreactors for the preparation of Fe-PBAs is limited, and microreactor design is mostly in the exploratory stage, making it challenging to achieve uniform and stable concentrations when mixing two liquid phases. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33 ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33 ref34" aria-label="reference 33 and 34">(33,34)</a></div><div class="NLM_p last">Herein, we introduce a T-shaped collision microreactor designed to significantly enhance the mixing rate in the liquid collision region, narrow the gap between it and the reaction rate, effectively eliminate the concentration gradient, and ensure air isolation. By addressing these principal challenges, the microreactor enables the continuous synthesis of low-defect Fe-PBAs using a liquid-phase precipitation method. The materials prepared in the microreactor were then compared to those prepared in traditional reactors to analyze the relationship between the microstructure characteristics of the product and its sodium storage performance. The Fe-PBAs synthesized in the microreactor possess low vacancies and high crystallinity, and it exhibits a specific capacity of 94.1 mAh/g at a current density of 0.5 C, with a capacity retention rate of 72.6% after 2000 cycles. The Coulombic efficiency of the cycling process was 100%. This work innovatively proposes the concept of matching mixing rate and reaction rate, adopting an efficient and fast preparation method that eliminates the need for protective gas, offering a new approach for the continuous production of high-quality Fe-PBAs.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Chemicals and Materials</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Ferrous sulfate heptahydrate (FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O, AR), sodium citrate dihydrate (C<sub>6</sub>H<sub>5</sub>Na<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O, AR), ascorbic acid (C<sub>6</sub>H<sub>8</sub>O<sub>6</sub>, AR), and anhydrous ethanol (C<sub>2</sub>H<sub>5</sub>OH, AR) were purchased from Chengdu Cologne Chemical Co., Ltd. Sodium ferrocyanide (Na<sub>4</sub>Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>, ≥98%) and <i>N</i>-methylpyrrolidone (NMP, C<sub>5</sub>H<sub>9</sub>NO, 99.5%) were purchased from Shanghai Aladdin Reagent Co., Ltd. Acetylene black was purchased from Cyber Electrochemical Materials Company. All reagents were not purified before use.</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Synthesis of Fe-PBA and Exploration of Synthetic Conditions</h3><div class="NLM_p">At a certain temperature,  Na<sub>4</sub>Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub> was dissolved in deionized water to obtain solution A.  FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O, sodium citrate, and ascorbic acid were dissolved in deionized water to obtain solution B. Then, solutions A and B were injected into the T-shaped collision microreactor through two inlets at the same rate using an injection pump for precipitation reaction. The mixture discharged from the microreactor outlet was aged for 12 h. After aging, the supernatant was poured out, the lower mixture was centrifuged, and it was washed three times with deionized water and anhydrous ethanol in sequence. Finally, the product was obtained by vacuum drying at 70 °C for 12 h. The preparation conditions for a series of Fe-PBA, including temperature, feed rate, and reactant concentration, are detailed in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table 1</a>, where the molar ratio of reactants Na<sub>4</sub>Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub> to FeSO<sub>4</sub> was consistently maintained at 1:1.2.</div><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Experiment Conditions for the Synthesis of the PBA Samples</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="table "><colgroup><col align="left"><col T-shaped collision microreactor used in this work is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>. The effects of equipment parameters (microreactor tube length and diameter), operating parameters (temperature, single feed flow rate, and reactant concentration), and additives (sodium citrate and ascorbic acid addition) on the preparation of Fe-PBA were explored. Fe-PBA was prepared under 14 different conditions, and the morphology of the material was characterized. These products are numbered as PBA-1, PBA-2, ..., and PBA-14. Under optimal conditions identified through this exploration, a comparative product was prepared in a flask, labeled as PBA-15. The raw materials for preparing PBA-15 were identical with the others. The preparation method is adding solution B dropwise to solution A, stirring for 2 h at 500 rpm, and then aging for 12 h. The subsequent centrifugal washing and drying steps were also consistent with those of the other samples.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c12929/asset/images/medium/am4c12929_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c12929/asset/images/large/am4c12929_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Schematic diagram of T-shaped collision microreactor (straight pipe with a length of 30 cm and an inner diameter of 0.5 mm).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c12929/asset/images/large/am4c12929_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c12929&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7">2.3.  Characterization of Materials</h3><div class="NLM_p">The Na and Fe content in all materials was determined by inductively coupled plasma (ICP-OES, 5100 SVDV, Agilent, America). The C and N content was determined through elemental analysis (EA, Vario EL Cube, Elemental, Germany). The water content was determined by thermogravimetric analysis (TG/DTG, METTLER TOLEDO, Switzerland). The phase structure of the materials was characterized by X-ray diffraction (XRD, EMPYREAN, PANalytical, The Netherlands). The chemical bonds in the material were identified by Fourier transform infrared spectrometry (FTIR, Spectrum One, Nicolet, America). The valence state of the iron element in the material was determined by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, K-Alpha, Thermo Scientific, America). The morphology of the crystal was observed by a scanning electron microscope (SEM, Helios G4 UC, TMO) and a transmission electron microscope (TEM, FEI Talos F200S). SEM images were acquired in a high-vacuum environment with an acceleration voltage set to 30 kV. TEM images were obtained with an accelerating voltage of 200 keV.</div><div class="NLM_p last">To evaluate the electrochemical performances of the Fe-PBA, CR2025 button cells were assembled by using the prepared powder as the positive electrode and metallic Na as the counter electrode. The positive electrode of the battery consists of Fe-PBA, acetylene black, and adhesive (NMP solution of PVDF with a mass fraction of 8%), with a mass ratio of 7:2:1 (based on the mass of PVDF). The electrolyte comprises a 1 mol/L NaClO<sub>4</sub> solution of ethylene carbonate/diethyl carbonate (EC/DEC, volume ratio 1:1). The batteries were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox and tested at room temperature. The constant current charging and discharging performance were examined on an electrochemical channel (CT-4008, NEWARE, China). Furthermore, the cyclic voltammetry curve (2–4.2 V, scan rate 0.1 mV/s) and AC impedance (10<sup>–2</sup>–10<sup>5</sup> Hz, amplitude 5 mV) were tested on an electrochemical workstation (CS2350, ARRTEST, China).</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i8">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec3_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i9" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i9">3.1.  Result of Conditional Exploration</h3><div id="sec3_1_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3"><div id="ac_i10" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h4 class="article-section__title" id="_i10">3.1.1.  Effect of Equipment Parameters</h4><div class="NLM_p">The SEM images of Fe-PBA prepared under different equipment parameter conditions are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>. As can be observed in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a-c, Fe-PBAs synthesized in microreactors with different tube lengths typically appear as irregular blocks with larger particle sizes. Surprisingly, there is no significant morphological change as the tube length increases. This finding may suggest that the synthesis reaction rate of Fe-PBA is exceptionally rapid and that the control step in its preparation process is not the precipitation reaction step, but rather the subsequent crystal growth step. Furthermore, as seen in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a and d, the degree of agglomeration  of Fe-PBA synthesized in microreactors with larger inner diameters noticeably increases, which can be explained by the fluid flow properties:<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-1"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-2"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-3"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-4"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-5">R</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-6">e</span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-7"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-8" style="margin-left: 0.333em;
