            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue and its analogs have received particular attention as superior cathodes for Na-ion batteries due to their potential 2-Na storage capacity (∼170 mA-h g-1) and low cost.  However, most of the Prussian blue compds. obtained from the conventional synthetic routes contain large amts. of Fe(CN)6 vacancies and coordinated H2O mols., which leads to the collapse of cyano-bridged framework and serious deterioration of their Na-storage ability.  Herein, the authors propose a facile citrate-assisted controlled crystn. method to obtain low-defect Prussian blue lattice with greatly improved Na-storage capacity and cycling stability.  As an example, the as-prepd. Na2CoFe(CN)6 nanocrystals demonstrate a reversible 2-Na storage reaction with a high specific capacity of 150 mA-h g-1 and a ∼ 90% capacity retention over 200 cycles, possibly serving as a low cost and high performance cathode for Na-ion batteries.  In particular, the synthetic strategy described in this work may be extended to other coordination-framework materials for a wide range of energy conversion and storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref20" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/cnma.201500021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vacancy-Free Prussian Blue Nanocrystals with High Capacity and Superior Cyclability for Aqueous Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemNanoMat</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">188</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">193</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vacancy-Free Prussian Blue Nanocrystals with High Capacity and Superior Cyclability for Aqueous Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xianyong; Sun, Mengying; Guo, Simin; Qian, Jiangfeng; Liu, Yong; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemNanoMat</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. Na-ion batteries have the competitive advantages of being low costing and possessing inherent safety, and they are particularly suitable for large-scale energy-storage applications.  However, the development of this new battery system is hindered by the lack of suitable Na hosts with sufficiently high capacity and cycle life.  Herein, we report vacancy-free Na2CoFe(CN)6 nanocubes synthesized by a controlled crystn. reaction and reveal their use as a new aq. cathode with reversible Na-storage behavior.  Owing to its perfect lattice framework with two redox-active sites, this material exhibits a high reversible capacity of 130 mA h g-1, a strong rate capability at 20 C, and superior cyclability with 90 % capacity retention over 800 cycles, all of which indicate that this material may possibly serve as a high-performance and long-life cathode for aq. Na-ion batteries.                 10.1016/j.electacta.2016.12.121</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D225%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D235-242%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DX.%2BYan%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DE.%2BLiu%26author%3DL.%2BSun%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DX.-Z.%2BLiao%26author%3DY.%2BHe%26author%3DZ.-F.%2BMa%26title%3DImproved%2BCycling%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BPrussian%2BBlue%2BCathode%2Bfor%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%2Bby%2BControlling%2BOperation%2BVoltage%2BRange%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2016.12.121&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2016.12.121&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved cycling performance of Prussian Blue cathode for sodium ion batteries by controlling operation voltage range</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Xiaomin; Yang, Yang; Liu, Ershuai; Sun, Liqi; Wang, Hong; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; He, Yushi; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">225</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">235-242</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue and its analogs were intensively studied as potential electrode materials for Na ion batteries.  A prussian blue sample was prepd. by a simple pptn. method and the electrochem. performance of the prussian blue (PB) cathode was studied at various temps. and in different voltage ranges.  When cycled in the voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V vs. Na/Na+, the PB cathode exhibited initial discharge capacities of 135.4 mAh g-1 (55°), 128.5 mAh g-1 (25°) and 99.2 mAh g-1 (-10°) at 10 mA g-1.  The PB cathode showed good cycling stability at low temp., however the cycling capacity degraded remarkably at elevated temp.  CV test indicated that the capacity fade was mainly due to the side reactions on the electrode-electrolyte interface at ∼4.0 V vs. Na/Na+.  XPS and FTIR analyses revealed several types of compds. formed on the cathode surface which indicated the complexity of the side reactions.  Controlling the high cut-off voltage at 3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ significantly improved the cycling stability of the PB electrode.  The PB cathode delivered 1C rate reversible capacity of 100.0 mAh g-1 in 2.0-3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ with outstanding capacity retention of 98.2% after 300 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2019.135533"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Low-Defect and Na-Enriched Prussian Blue Lattice with Ultralong Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>332</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">135533</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2019.135533</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D332%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DC.%2BYan%26author%3DA.%2BZhao%26author%3DF.%2BZhong%26author%3DX.%2BFeng%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26author%3DJ.%2BQian%26author%3DX.%2BAi%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BCao%26title%3DA%2BLow-Defect%2Band%2BNa-Enriched%2BPrussian%2BBlue%2BLattice%2Bwith%2BUltralong%2BCycle%2BLife%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BCathode%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2019.135533&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2019.135533&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A low-defect and Na-enriched Prussian blue lattice with ultralong cycle life for sodium-ion battery cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Changxiu; Zhao, Along; Zhong, Faping; Feng, Xiangming; Chen, Weihua; Qian, Jiangfeng; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">332</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">135533</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue compds. were considered as attractive candidate cathodes for Na ion battery (SIB) due to open channel structure, tunable chem. compns. and potential high capacity.  However, their low capacity use and insufficient cyclability have hindered their large-scale applications.  Na-enrich PB lattices (NaxFe[Fe(CN)6]1-y·zH2O) with different contents of [Fe(CN)6] vacancies and coordinated H2O were synthesized to study the effects of the lattice defects on the reversible capacities and cycling stabilities of the PB materials.  Decreasing the content of structural defects can greatly elevate the electrochem. performance of the PB cathodes.  The as prepd. low-defect and Na+-enriched Na1.81Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.83·2.04H2O lattice can achieve a high reversible capacity of &gt;140 mAh g-1, a superior rate capability with 55.2% of its initial capacity at 10 C and a long-term cyclability with 78% capacity retention over 3700 cycles, possibly serving as a low cost, high capacity and cycle-stable cathode for Na ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.01.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium storage in Na-rich Na<sub>x</sub>FeFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> nanocubes</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">386</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">393</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.01.012</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D386-393%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BQiao%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26author%3DL.%2BMiao%26author%3DL.%2BYuan%26author%3DX.%2BHu%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26title%3DSodium%2Bstorage%2Bin%2BNa-rich%2BNaxFeFe%2528CN%25296%2Bnanocubes%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2015.01.012&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2015.01.012&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium storage in Na-rich NaxFeFe(CN)6 nanocubes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yang; Qiao, Yun; Zhang, Wuxing; Li, Zhen; Ji, Xiao; Miao, Ling; Yuan, Lixia; Hu, Xianluo; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">386-393</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-rich prussian blue analogs (PBs) with high coulombic efficiency are of fundamental and technol. importance for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Here we report high-quality NaxFeFe(CN)6 nanocubes as cathode materials for SIBs and investigate their sodium storage mechanism.  Among them, Na-rich Na1.70FeFe(CN)6 shows highly reversible electrochem. reactions, delivering a capacity as high as 120.7 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1; even at 1200 mA g-1, the capacity still retains up to 73.6 mA h g-1.  The first-cycle coulombic efficiency strongly depends on the sodium content in NaxFeFe(CN)6.  Exptl. results and first-principle calcns. demonstrate that sodium cations in the large cavities of PBs have a priority to occupy the 8c site, while in the Na-rich samples, Na+ ions can be pushed into other 24d site.  We believe that our findings can provide new insights into sodium storage mechanism for the PBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.jssc.2013.11.013"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis of Layered Double Hydroxide Nanosheets by Coprecipitation Using a T-type Microchannel Reactor</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of layered double hydroxide nanosheets by coprecipitation using a T-type microchannel reactor</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pang, Xiujiang; Sun, Meiyu; Ma, Xiuming; Hou, Wanguo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">210</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">111-115</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The synthesis of Mg2Al-NO3 layered double hydroxide (LDH) nanosheets by copptn. using a T-type microchannel reactor is reported.  Aq. LDH nanosheet dispersions were obtained.  The LDH nanosheets were characterized by X-ray diffraction, transmission electron microscopy, at. force microscopy, and particle size anal., and the transmittance and viscosity of LDH nanosheet dispersions were examd.  The two-dimensional LDH nanosheets consisted of 1-2 brucite-like layers and were stable for ca. 16 h at room temp.  In addn., the co-assembly between LDH nanosheets and dodecyl sulfate (DS) anions was carried out, and a DS intercalated LDH nano-hybrid was obtained.  This simple, cheap method can provide naked LDH nanosheets in high quantities, which can be used as building blocks for functional materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref31" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1039/c1cc00089f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wiles, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Watts, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Micro Reaction Technology</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible structural evolution of sodium-rich rhombohedral Prussian blue for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Wanlin; Gang, Yong; Hu, Zhe; Yan, Zichao; Li, Weijie; Li, Yongcheng; Gu, Qin-Fen; Wang, Zhixing; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron-based Prussian blue analogs are promising low-cost and easily prepd. cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Their materials quality and electrochem. performance are heavily reliant on the pptn. process.  Here we report a controllable pptn. method to synthesize high-performance Prussian blue for sodium-ion storage.  Characterization of the nucleation and evolution processes of the highly cryst. Prussian blue microcubes reveals a rhombohedral structure that exhibits high initial Coulombic efficiency, excellent rate performance, and cycling properties.  The phase transitions in the as-obtained material are investigated by synchrotron in situ powder X-ray diffraction, which shows highly reversible structural transformations between rhombohedral, cubic, and tetragonal structures upon sodium-ion (de)intercalations.  Moreover, the Prussian blue material from a large-scale synthesis process shows stable cycling performance in a pouch full cell over 1000 times.  We believe that this work could pave the way for the real application of Prussian blue materials in sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.202200404"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, C. L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sub>1.51</sub>Fe[Fe(CN)<sub>6</sub>]<sub>0.87</sub>·1.83H<sub>2</sub>O Hollow Nanospheres via Non-Aqueous Ball-Milling Route to Achieve High Initial Coulombic Efficiency and High Rate Capability in Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e2200404</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smtd.202200404</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DSmall%2BMethods%26issue%3D8%26author%3DC.%2BM.%2BXu%26author%3DJ.%2BPeng%26author%3DX.%2BH.%2BLiu%26author%3DW.%2BH.%2BLai%26author%3DX.%2BX.%2BHe%26author%3DZ.%2BYang%26author%3DJ.%2BZ.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BQiao%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BL.%2BChou%26title%3DNa1.51Fe%255BFe%2528CN%25296%255D0.87%25C2%25B71.83H2O%2BHollow%2BNanospheres%2Bvia%2BNon-Aqueous%2BBall-Milling%2BRoute%2Bto%2BAchieve%2BHigh%2BInitial%2BCoulombic%2BEfficiency%2Band%2BHigh%2BRate%2BCapability%2Bin%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmtd.202200404&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmtd.202200404&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1149/2.0031610jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.-F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Influence of structural imperfection on electrochemical behavior of prussian blue cathode materials for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Electrochem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>163</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">9</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">A2117</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">A2123</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/2.0031610jes</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D163%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3DA2117-A2123%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectrochem.%2BSoc.%26issue%3D9%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DE.%2BLiu%26author%3DX.%2BYan%26author%3DC.%2BMa%26author%3DW.%2BWen%26author%3DX.-Z.%2BLiao%26author%3DZ.-F.%2BMa%26title%3DInfluence%2Bof%2Bstructural%2Bimperfection%2Bon%2Belectrochemical%2Bbehavior%2Bof%2Bprussian%2Bblue%2Bcathode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1149%252F2.0031610jes&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1149%2F2.0031610jes&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Influence of Structural Imperfection on Electrochemical Behavior of Prussian Blue Cathode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Yang; Liu, Ershuai; Yan, Xiaomin; Ma, Chunrong; Wen, Wen; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">163</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A2117-A2123</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue compds. (PBs) have been intensely studied as promising cathode materials for Na ion batteries due to their rigid open framework which benefits Na+ insertion/extn.  However, the existence of Fe(CN)6 vacancies occupied by coordinating H2O in the framework has great influence on the electrochem. performance.  The authors prepd. PB compds. using simple soln. pptn. method at 0°, 40°C and 80°C, resp.  The obtained Na1.73Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.98.box.0.02 (PB0), Na1.27Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.94.box.0.06 (PB40) and Na1.12Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.92.box.0.08 (PB80) samples were studied to clarify the effects of Fe(CN)6 vacancies and the coordinating H2O mols. on the electrochem. behavior.  CV tests indicated that coordinating H2O could be gradually extd. and attend side reaction at ∼4.0V, which led to impedance growth and caused capacity decrease during cycling.  Dehydrated PB samples showed increased reversible capacities.  However, the cycling stability of the PBs mainly depended on the perfection of the lattice structure.  Low defect structure Na1.73Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.98.box.0.02 exhibited superior cycling stability with initial reversible capacity of 105 mA h g-1 (100 mA g-1) and intact cubic phase lattice structure during long term cycling.  Dehydrated Na1.73Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.98.box.0.02 showed further improved reversible capacities of 123 mA h g-1 (100 mA g-1) with 73% capacity retention after 200 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref44" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Activation of Sodium Storage Sites in Prussian Blue Analogues via Surface Etching</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">4713</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4718</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D17%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D4713-4718%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26issue%3D8%26author%3DW.%2BRen%26author%3DM.%2BQin%26author%3DZ.%2BZhu%26author%3DM.%2BYan%26author%3DQ.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BZhang%26author%3DD.%2BLiu%26author%3DL.%2BMai%26title%3DActivation%2Bof%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BSites%2Bin%2BPrussian%2BBlue%2BAnalogues%2Bvia%2BSurface%2BEtching%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.7b01366&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.7b01366&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Activation of Sodium Storage Sites in Prussian Blue Analogues via Surface Etching</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ren, Wenhao; Qin, Mingsheng; Zhu, Zixuan; Yan, Mengyu; Li, Qi; Zhang, Lei; Liu, Dongna; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4713-4718</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion battery technologies are known to suffer from kinetic problems assocd. with the solid-state diffusion of Na+ in intercalation electrodes, which results in suppressed specific capacity and degraded rate performance.  Here, a controllable selective etching approach is developed for the synthesis of Prussian blue analog (PBA) with enhanced sodium storage activity.  On the basis of time-dependent expts., a defect-induced morphol. evolution mechanism from nanocube to nanoflower structure is proposed.  Through in situ X-ray diffraction measurement and computational anal., this unique structure is revealed to provide higher Na+ diffusion dynamics and negligible vol. change during the sodiation/desodiation processes.  As a sodium ion battery cathode, the PBA exhibits a discharge capacity of 90 mA h g-1, which is in good agreement with the complete low spin FeLS(C) redox reaction.  It also demonstrates an outstanding rate capability of 71.0 mA h g-1 at 44.4 C, as well as an unprecedented cycling reversibility over 5000 times.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/nl203193q"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wessells, C. D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peddada, S. V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huggins, R. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nickel Hexacyanoferrate Nanoparticle Electrodes for Aqueous Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">5421</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl203193q</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D5421-5%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26issue%3D12%26author%3DC.%2BD.%2BWessells%26author%3DS.%2BV.%2BPeddada%26author%3DR.%2BA.%2BHuggins%26author%3DY.%2BCui%26title%3DNickel%2BHexacyanoferrate%2BNanoparticle%2BElectrodes%2Bfor%2BAqueous%2BSodium%2Band%2BPotassium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnl203193q&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnl203193q&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nickel Hexacyanoferrate Nanoparticle Electrodes For Aqueous Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wessells, Colin D.; Peddada, Sandeep V.; Huggins, Robert A.; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5421-5425</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The elec. power grid faces a growing need for large-scale energy storage over a wide range of time scales due to costly short-term transients, frequency regulation, and load balancing.  The durability, high power, energy efficiency, and low cost needed for grid-scale storage pose substantial challenges for conventional battery technol.  Here, we demonstrate insertion/extn. of sodium and potassium ions in a low-strain nickel hexacyanoferrate electrode material for at least five thousand deep cycles at high current densities in inexpensive aq. electrolytes.  Its open-framework structure allows retention of 66% of the initial capacity even at a high (41.7C) rate.  At low current densities, its round trip energy efficiency reaches 99%.  This low-cost material is readily synthesized in bulk quantities.  The long cycle life, high power, good energy efficiency, safety, and inexpensive prodn. method make nickel hexacyanoferrate an attractive candidate for use in large-scale batteries to support the elec. grid.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201800259"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, F.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X. Z.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z. F.</span></span>, <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Hollow Prussian Blue Rods Synthesized via Self-Sacrifice Template as Cathode for High Performance Sodium Ion Battery</span>.  <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume">3</span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>).<span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smtd.201800259</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2019%26journal%3DSmall%2BMethods%26issue%3D4%26author%3DF.%2BFeng%26author%3DS.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BZ.%2BLiao%26author%3DZ.%2BF.%2BMa%26title%3DHierarchical%2BHollow%2BPrussian%2BBlue%2BRods%2BSynthesized%2Bvia%2BSelf-Sacrifice%2BTemplate%2Bas%2BCathode%2Bfor%2BHigh%2BPerformance%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmtd.201800259&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c12929&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmtd.201800259&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                10.1002/adfm.201909530</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Cathode Choice for Commercialization of Sodium-Ion Batteries: Layered Transition Metal Oxides versus Prussian Blue Analogs</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Qiannan; Hu, Zhe; Chen, Mingzhe; Zou, Chao; Jin, Huile; Wang, Shun; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Yong; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1909530</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  With the unprecedentedly increasing demand for renewable and clean energy sources, the sodium-ion battery (SIB) is emerging as an alternative or complementary energy storage candidate to the present com. lithium-ion battery due to the abundance and low cost of sodium resources.  Layered transition metal oxides and Prussian blue analogs are reviewed in terms of their com. potential as cathode materials for SIBs.  The recent progress in research on their half cells and full cells for the ultimate application in SIBs are summarized.  In addn., their electrochem. performance, suitability for scaling up, cost, and environmental concerns are compared in detail with a brief outlook on future prospects.  It is anticipated that this review will inspire further development of layered transition metal oxides and Prussian blue analogs for SIBs, esp. for their emerging commercialization.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE44004D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Quality Prussian Blue Crystals as Superior Cathode Materials for Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electrolyte design or functional development is very effective at promoting the performance of sodium-ion batteries, which are attractive for electrochem. energy storage devices due to abundant sodium resources and low cost.  This review discusses recent advances on electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries and comprehensive electrolyte design strategies for various materials systems as well as functional applications.  The discussion is divided into three electrolyte types: liq., solid state, and gel state.  Liq. electrolytes are further divided into different solvent types, including org. carbonate ester, ether, ionic liq., and water.  Solid-state electrolytes also contain two types: solid polymer and glass-ceramic composite.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As a promising alternative to the market-leading lithium-ion batteries, low-cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are attractive for applications such as large-scale elec. energy storage systems.  The energy d., cycling life, and rate performance of SIBs are fundamentally dependent on dynamic physiochem. reactions, structural change, and morphol. evolution.  Therefore, it is essential to holistically understand SIBs reaction processes, degrdn. mechanisms, and thermal/mech. behaviors in complex working environments.  The recent developments of advanced in situ and operando characterization enable the establishment of the structure- processing- property- performance relationship in SIBs under operating conditions.  This Review summarizes significant recent progress in SIBs exploiting in situ and operando techniques based on X-ray and electron analyses at different time and length scales.  Through the combination of spectroscopy, imaging, and diffraction, local and global changes in SIBs can be elucidated for improving materials design.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The oxygen stacking of O3-type layered sodium transition metal oxides (O3-NaTMO2) changes dynamically upon topotactic Na extn. and reinsertion.  While the phase transition from octahedral to prismatic Na coordination that occurs at intermediate desodiation by transition metal slab gliding is well understood, the structural evolution at high desodiation, crucial to achieve high reversible capacity, remains mostly uncharted.  In this work, the phase transitions of O3-type layered NaTMO2 at high voltage are investigated by combining exptl. and computational approaches.  An OP2-type phase that consists of alternating octahedral and prismatic Na layers is directly obsd. by in situ X-ray diffraction and high-resoln. scanning transmission electron microscopy.  The origin of this peculiar phase is explained by at. interactions involving Jahn-Teller active Fe4+ and distortion tolerant Ti4+ that stabilize the local Na environment.  The path-dependent desodiation and resodiation pathways are also rationalized in this material through the different kinetics of the prismatic and octahedral layers, presenting a comprehensive picture about the structural stability of the layered materials upon Na intercalation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref13" class="rightTabRefNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit13" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA08991H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tripathi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rudola, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gajjela, S.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2(PO4)2F3 (NVPF) with NASCION (Na superionic conductor) is recognized as a potential cathode material owing to its high theor. capacity.  However, the electronic cond. of NVPF is much lower than its ionic cond., which seriously affects the properties of this material.  The carbon layer can be used as the conductive medium to enhance the cond. of NVPF.  In this study, we propose a single-step solid-state reaction method based on mech. activation with pitch as the carbon source to synthesize NVPF/C composites.  The crystallog. structure and morphol. of all as-prepd. samples were investigated by XRD, Raman spectroscopy, BET measurement, thermal anal., SEM and TEM.  Furthermore, the electrochem. performance and kinetic properties were analyzed by CV, galvanostatic charge-discharge and EIS tests.  These tests outcomes demonstrated that the NVPF/C-2 composite with a carbon content of 12.14 wt% showed an excellent rate performance and cycle stability.  It presented reversible capacities of 103 and 95 mA h g-1 at 0.2 and 10C, resp., and an outstanding retention of 91.9% after 500 cycles at 5C.  These excellent properties of the NVPF/C-2 composite are attributed to its high ion diffusion coeff. and small charge transfer impedance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1149/1.1523691"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Barker, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saidi, M. Y.; Swoyer, J. L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemical and Solid-State Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Preliminary performance data is presented for a novel sodium-ion cell based on a hard carbon/NaVPO4F chem.  To our knowledge this is the first time that a viable sodium-ion system based on a polyanion cathode material has been demonstrated.  The NaVPO4F was prepd. by a simple incorporation reaction involving vanadium(III) phosphate, VPO4 and NaF.  The hard carbon was from a com. source.  Const. current cycling indicated reversible alkali-ion insertion behavior for the fluorophosphate material, while the generally sym. nature of the charge/discharge curves indicated the energetic reversibility of the insertion system.  The av. discharge voltage for the sodium-ion cells was demonstrated to around 3.7 V, a figure comparable with com. available lithium-ion cells.  The reversible specific capacities for the cathode and anode active materials were detd. to be 82 and 202 mAh/g, resp.  Representative test cells cycled more than 30 times before their discharge capacity had declined to less then 50% of the original.  The relatively high first cycle charge inefficiency is thought to be due to irreversible passivation reactions occurring at the carbon surface.  Significant performance enhancements may be made by optimization of the electrolyte system and improving the active material mass balance.  In summary, low overvoltage, good insertion reversibility, and reasonable capacity retention characterize this fluorophosphate-based sodium-ion cell.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.jssc.2019.06.027"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gond, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meena, S.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue and its analogs have received particular attention as superior cathodes for Na-ion batteries due to their potential 2-Na storage capacity (∼170 mA-h g-1) and low cost.  However, most of the Prussian blue compds. obtained from the conventional synthetic routes contain large amts. of Fe(CN)6 vacancies and coordinated H2O mols., which leads to the collapse of cyano-bridged framework and serious deterioration of their Na-storage ability.  Herein, the authors propose a facile citrate-assisted controlled crystn. method to obtain low-defect Prussian blue lattice with greatly improved Na-storage capacity and cycling stability.  As an example, the as-prepd. Na2CoFe(CN)6 nanocrystals demonstrate a reversible 2-Na storage reaction with a high specific capacity of 150 mA-h g-1 and a ∼ 90% capacity retention over 200 cycles, possibly serving as a low cost and high performance cathode for Na-ion batteries.  In particular, the synthetic strategy described in this work may be extended to other coordination-framework materials for a wide range of energy conversion and storage applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1002/cnma.201500021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vacancy-Free Prussian Blue Nanocrystals with High Capacity and Superior Cyclability for Aqueous Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemNanoMat</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">188</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">193</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aq. Na-ion batteries have the competitive advantages of being low costing and possessing inherent safety, and they are particularly suitable for large-scale energy-storage applications.  However, the development of this new battery system is hindered by the lack of suitable Na hosts with sufficiently high capacity and cycle life.  Herein, we report vacancy-free Na2CoFe(CN)6 nanocubes synthesized by a controlled crystn. reaction and reveal their use as a new aq. cathode with reversible Na-storage behavior.                         rightTab-cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved cycling performance of Prussian Blue cathode for sodium ion batteries by controlling operation voltage range</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Xiaomin; Yang, Yang; Liu, Ershuai; Sun, Liqi; Wang, Hong; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; He, Yushi; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue and its analogs were intensively studied as potential electrode materials for Na ion batteries.  A prussian blue sample was prepd. by a simple pptn. method and the electrochem. performance of the prussian blue (PB) cathode was studied at various temps. and in different voltage ranges.  When cycled in the voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V vs. Na/Na+, the PB cathode exhibited initial discharge capacities of 135.4 mAh g-1 (55°), 128.5 mAh g-1 (25°) and 99.2 mAh g-1 (-10°) at 10 mA g-1.  The PB cathode showed good cycling stability at low temp., however the cycling capacity degraded remarkably at elevated temp.  CV test indicated that the capacity fade was mainly due to the side reactions on the electrode-electrolyte interface at ∼4.0 V vs. Na/Na+.  XPS and FTIR analyses revealed several types of compds. formed on the cathode surface which indicated the complexity of the side reactions.  Controlling the high cut-off voltage at 3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ significantly improved the cycling stability of the PB electrode.  The PB cathode delivered 1C rate reversible capacity of 100.0 mAh g-1 in 2.0-3.8 V vs. Na/Na+ with outstanding capacity retention of 98.2% after 300 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2019.135533"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Low-Defect and Na-Enriched Prussian Blue Lattice with Ultralong Cycle Life for Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue compds. were considered as attractive candidate cathodes for Na ion battery (SIB) due to open channel structure, tunable chem. compns. and potential high capacity.  However, their low capacity use and insufficient cyclability have hindered their large-scale applications.  Na-enrich PB lattices (NaxFe[Fe(CN)6]1-y·zH2O) with different contents of [Fe(CN)6] vacancies and coordinated H2O were synthesized to study the effects of the lattice defects on the reversible capacities and cycling stabilities of the PB materials.  Decreasing the content of structural defects can greatly elevate the electrochem. performance of the PB cathodes.  The as prepd. low-defect and Na+-enriched Na1.81Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.83·2.04H2O lattice can achieve a high reversible capacity of &gt;140 mAh g-1, a superior rate capability with 55.2% of its initial capacity at 10 C and a long-term cyclability with 78% capacity retention over 3700 cycles, possibly serving as a low cost, high capacity and cycle-stable cathode for Na ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.01.012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium storage in Na-rich Na<sub>x</sub>FeFe(CN)<sub>6</sub> nanocubes</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">386</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">393</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-rich prussian blue analogs (PBs) with high coulombic efficiency are of fundamental and technol. importance for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Here we report high-quality NaxFeFe(CN)6 nanocubes as cathode materials for SIBs and investigate their sodium storage mechanism.  Among them, Na-rich Na1.70FeFe(CN)6 shows highly reversible electrochem. reactions, delivering a capacity as high as 120.7 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 200 mA g-1; even at 1200 mA g-1, the capacity still retains up to 73.6 mA h g-1.  The first-cycle coulombic efficiency strongly depends on the sodium content in NaxFeFe(CN)6.  Exptl. results and first-principle calcns. demonstrate that sodium cations in the large cavities of PBs have a priority to occupy the 8c site, while in the Na-rich samples, Na+ ions can be pushed into other 24d site.                         rightTab-cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible structural evolution of sodium-rich rhombohedral Prussian blue for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Wanlin; Gang, Yong; Hu, Zhe; Yan, Zichao; Li, Weijie; Li, Yongcheng; Gu, Qin-Fen; Wang, Zhixing; Chou, Shu-Lei; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron-based Prussian blue analogs are promising low-cost and easily prepd. cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Their materials quality and electrochem. performance are heavily reliant on the pptn. process.  Here we report a controllable pptn. method to synthesize high-performance Prussian blue for sodium-ion storage.  Characterization of the nucleation and evolution processes of the highly cryst. Prussian blue microcubes reveals a rhombohedral structure that exhibits high initial Coulombic efficiency, excellent rate performance, and cycling properties.  The phase transitions in the as-obtained material are investigated by synchrotron in situ powder X-ray diffraction, which shows highly reversible structural transformations between rhombohedral, cubic, and tetragonal structures upon sodium-ion (de)intercalations.  Moreover, the Prussian blue material from a large-scale synthesis process shows stable cycling performance in a pouch full cell over 1000 times.  We believe that this work could pave the way for the real application of Prussian blue materials in sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref42" class="rightTabRefNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit42" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.202200404"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, C.                         rightTab-cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Influence of Structural Imperfection on Electrochemical Behavior of Prussian Blue Cathode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Yang; Liu, Ershuai; Yan, Xiaomin; Ma, Chunrong; Wen, Wen; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">163</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue compds. (PBs) have been intensely studied as promising cathode materials for Na ion batteries due to their rigid open framework which benefits Na+ insertion/extn.  However, the existence of Fe(CN)6 vacancies occupied by coordinating H2O in the framework has great influence on the electrochem. performance.  The authors prepd. PB compds. using simple soln. pptn. method at 0°, 40°C and 80°C, resp.  The obtained Na1.73Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.98.box.0.02 (PB0), Na1.27Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.94.box.0.06 (PB40) and Na1.12Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.92.box.0.08 (PB80) samples were studied to clarify the effects of Fe(CN)6 vacancies and the coordinating H2O mols. on the electrochem. behavior.  CV tests indicated that coordinating H2O could be gradually extd. and attend side reaction at ∼4.0V, which led to impedance growth and caused capacity decrease during cycling.  Dehydrated PB samples showed increased reversible capacities.  However, the cycling stability of the PBs mainly depended on the perfection of the lattice structure.  Low defect structure Na1.73Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.98.box.0.02 exhibited superior cycling stability with initial reversible capacity of 105 mA h g-1 (100 mA g-1) and intact cubic phase lattice structure during long term cycling.  Dehydrated Na1.73Fe[Fe(CN)6]0.98.box.0.02 showed further improved reversible capacities of 123 mA h g-1 (100 mA g-1) with 73% capacity retention after 200 cycles.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref44" class="rightTabRefNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit44" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Activation of Sodium Storage Sites in Prussian Blue Analogues via Surface Etching</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">4713</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4718</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.7b01366</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Activation of Sodium Storage Sites in Prussian Blue Analogues via Surface Etching</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ren, Wenhao; Qin, Mingsheng; Zhu, Zixuan; Yan, Mengyu; Li, Qi; Zhang, Lei; Liu, Dongna; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion battery technologies are known to suffer from kinetic problems assocd. with the solid-state diffusion of Na+ in intercalation electrodes, which results in suppressed specific capacity and degraded rate performance.  Here, a controllable selective etching approach is developed for the synthesis of Prussian blue analog (PBA) with enhanced sodium storage activity.  On the basis of time-dependent expts., a defect-induced morphol. evolution mechanism from nanocube to nanoflower structure is proposed.  Through in situ X-ray diffraction measurement and computational anal., this unique structure is revealed to provide higher Na+ diffusion dynamics and negligible vol. change during the sodiation/desodiation processes.  As a sodium ion battery cathode, the PBA exhibits a discharge capacity of 90 mA h g-1, which is in good agreement with the complete low spin FeLS(C) redox reaction.  It also demonstrates an outstanding rate capability of 71.0 mA h g-1 at 44.4 C, as well as an unprecedented cycling reversibility over 5000 times.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1021/nl203193q"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wessells, C. D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peddada, S. V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huggins, R. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nickel Hexacyanoferrate Nanoparticle Electrodes for Aqueous Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">5421</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nl203193q</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nickel Hexacyanoferrate Nanoparticle Electrodes For Aqueous Sodium and Potassium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wessells, Colin D.; Peddada, Sandeep V.; Huggins, Robert A.; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5421-5425</span>CODEN:

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The elec. power grid faces a growing need for large-scale energy storage over a wide range of time scales due to costly short-term transients, frequency regulation, and load balancing.  The durability, high power, energy efficiency, and low cost needed for grid-scale storage pose substantial challenges for conventional battery technol.  Here, we demonstrate insertion/extn. of sodium and potassium ions in a low-strain nickel hexacyanoferrate electrode material for at least five thousand deep cycles at high current densities in inexpensive aq. electrolytes.  Its open-framework structure allows retention of 66% of the initial capacity even at a high (41.7C) rate.  At low current densities, its round trip energy efficiency reaches 99%.  This low-cost material is readily synthesized in bulk quantities.  The long cycle life, high power, good energy efficiency, safety, and inexpensive prodn. method make nickel hexacyanoferrate an attractive candidate for use in large-scale batteries to support the elec. grid.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref46" class="rightTabRefNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit46" data-doi="10.1002/smtd.201800259"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, F.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X. Z.</span>; <span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z. F.</span></span>, <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Hollow Prussian Blue Rods Synthesized via Self-Sacrifice Template as Cathode for High Performance Sodium Ion Battery</span>.  <i>Small Methods</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume">3</span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>).<span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        <script nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

        errorStatus = false,

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);

        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>

        <script nonce="931885469c1d54b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
